  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_54666ba1-cbf9-4dd9-a905-a9bb4d1325cc'
      });

  <span id="freeText17086189135204450326" style="display:none">Hailed as “impossible to put down,” the Hex Hall series has both critics and teens cheering. With a winning combination of romance, action, magic and humor, this third volume will leave readers enchanted.<br /><br />Just as Sophie Mercer has come to accept her extraordinary magical powers as a demon, the Prodigium Council strips them away. Now Sophie is defenseless, alone, and at the mercy of her sworn enemies—the Brannicks, a family of warrior women who hunt down the Prodigium. Or at least that’s what Sophie thinks, until she makes a surprising discovery. The Brannicks know an epic war is coming, and they believe Sophie is the only one powerful enough to stop the world from ending. But without her magic, Sophie isn’t as confident.<br /><br />Sophie’s bound for one hell of a ride—can she get her powers back before it’s too late?</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=pn-shapeshifters">pn-shapeshifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=read-2012">read-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=huge-disappointments">huge-disappointments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=pn-witches">pn-witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=brain-candy">brain-candy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer165756360" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17210259895346758054">**<b>Please be aware that the spoilers in this review are real</b>, so don't click on them unless you've read the book. There are mild spoilers in the visible text, but they're not anything that you haven't already guessed if you're already a fan of the series. And since three people have done this already, please <b>DO NOT discuss spoilers in this book without spoiler-tagging your comments</b> since you will absolutely ruin the book for people who haven't read the book yet. If you don't know how to do this, </span>
  <span id="freeText17210259895346758054" style="display:none">**<b>Please be aware that the spoilers in this review are real</b>, so don't click on them unless you've read the book. There are mild spoilers in the visible text, but they're not anything that you haven't already guessed if you're already a fan of the series. And since three people have done this already, please <b>DO NOT discuss spoilers in this book without spoiler-tagging your comments</b> since you will absolutely ruin the book for people who haven't read the book yet. If you don't know how to do this, please learn before commenting.**<br /><br />I absolutely LOVED the first two Hex Hall novels. There are few authors whose books I pounce on at midnight the day of release and stay up all night reading, so that should give you an idea of how much I love Sophie, Jenna, Archer, and Cal.<br /><br />The relationship between Sophie and Jenna is still fantastic, and that was probably my favorite part of this book. Their worry for each other, their banter, etc, are all familiar and funny and a welcome interlude whenever they're together. There is also a plot line involving <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[demon kids Nick and Daisy that pulled at my heartstrings a bit. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I'm sorry to say that this turned out to be my least favorite book in the series, however. The action zips back and forth between a lot of locations and the various overlapping storylines felt rather jumbled, which is problematic even if you've already guessed many of the big secrets back when you were reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8428064.Demonglass__Hex_Hall___2_" title="Demonglass (Hex Hall, #2) by Rachel Hawkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Demonglass</a>. I had a hard time staying engaged in the story, especially since there were moments that seemed to lend themselves to a bigger emotional punch <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[such as the revelation that her mom is a Brannick, the early interactions with Cal, seeing her father again, Archer being tortured, etc <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> than were portrayed. I also got a little tired of Elodie popping up again and again <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and possessing Sophie's body <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and the way Sophie's magic came and went at pretty convenient moments.<br /><br />My two biggest issues with the book, however, were: <br /><br />1. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Sophie kissing Cal <i>very</i> soon after the book begins, before she even knows if something's happened to Archer. I'm not satisfied with the amount of guilt she felt after Archer pops up again, and in fact, she never even tells him about that particular kiss. Then Elodie later uses Sophie's body to kiss Cal again to torture Archer! Both scenarios just seemed very convoluted and forced to me, and they felt very different from the sunny nature of the previous books. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />2. DO NOT CLICK THIS if you haven't read the book. Seriously. Don't do it. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Cal's death. And the precious little amount of time spent mourning him. Please give me a hug. :(  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Not only did that make me extremely sad, but it felt so unnecessary.<br /><br />Many of the elements I enjoyed so much about the previous books just felt different here. It's definitely still a funny book, but there's so much going on that the humor doesn't flow quite as smoothly. The parental relationships, always one of the stronger parts of the Hex Hall and Demonglass, were largely absent here as well. And most of all, there's very little time spent with Archer or Cal. What's there relies a tremendous amount on your past knowledge of Sophie's intimacy with them, and there aren't nearly enough meaningful moments between them for my taste. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Okay, and not nearly enough make out scenes, either! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Don't get me wrong, there are <i>some</i>, but they didn't seem as urgent and charged as the ones in the previous books. <br /><br />Maybe it's just me? I'm really sad to feel this way about the ending of a series I love so much. I'm very curious to see what my fellow Sophie fans think of this one, though. I liked this book overall, but the surprises that this book offered were just not the kind that I really enjoyed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17210259895346758054" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer148133986" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17887329323373056954">Review, March 15:<br/><br/>As much as it literally hurts rating this book four stars, I have to do it. I will admit to anyone who wants to hear that I have pretty much been obsessively waiting for this ending since I read Hex Hall on my birthday two years ago. Really. I have waited so long, and as much as I want to say it was perfect it wasn't.<br/><br/>Not to say it wasn't enjoyable. In fact, I absolutly love it. I love the humor, I love the twist in Part two. I adore Sophie, Archer, Jenna, and Cal, and I so wish </span>
  <span id="freeText17887329323373056954" style="display:none">Review, March 15:<br /><br />As much as it literally hurts rating this book four stars, I have to do it. I will admit to anyone who wants to hear that I have pretty much been obsessively waiting for this ending since I read Hex Hall on my birthday two years ago. Really. I have waited so long, and as much as I want to say it was perfect it wasn't.<br /><br />Not to say it wasn't enjoyable. In fact, I absolutly love it. I love the humor, I love the twist in Part two. I adore Sophie, Archer, Jenna, and Cal, and I so wish that my parents were as totally cute as James and Grace are. But there are simply to many factors that take away from the book that make it a four star book for me.<br /><br />First off, the Brannicks. I have been waiting to find out what was going on with them since Demonglass, yet I feel that we hardly saw them. I did like the plot twist in Part Two, but that made us leave the Brannicks so abruptly, I was disappointed. I thought the book was going to be about Sophie learning how to kick butt via Brannick teachings, yet that didn't happen. We get to see some background information and meet the Brannicks, but then they are gone until much later in the book. I don't even feel like they were even fleshed out much. Even Izzy wasn't made much of a character.<br /><br />Then, there was the big battle sequence at the end. So, I am not going to spoil anything here, but I will say that it was a big disappointment. Think Mockingjay conflicts, where Katniss passes out during the really exciting parts. No, Sophie doesn't pass out until the end, but the whole battle was super short and way too easy. You'll see what I mean when you read it. I was looking forward to a epic battle, good vs. evil, that sort of thing, and again it didn't happen.<br /><br />Last of all, the love triangle. The following information is covered with the spoiler cover for a reason, so don't read it unless you want to see me rant on that. You have been warned.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When I read Mockingjay, the one and only time I read it, I found myself hoping that the loser of Katniss's heart would sacrifice himself for Katniss. Well, God answered my plea, only in this book instead of that one. Racheal Hawkins kills Cal. Holy Hell Weasel. I didn't think she would have the guts to do it. It's actually probably the only thing about this book I'm completly content with if I want to be honest. Not that I was hoping Cal would die. I wasn't chanting that or anything during the book. However, it was almost romantic in a way, Cal healing Sophie and getting himself killed to save her life. It made me feel really sorry and actually care for him. I do think that Hawkins should have done him more justice though. I didn't think about Cal in the first book, and when she introduced him as a love intrest, I hated, well, disliked him. I'm in love Archer, and I still think the love triangle was pointless. <br /><br />Also, one more complaint, I wanted to see more of Sophie's parents. They are just so adorable together! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Now that that's out of the way. I just want to say that I did enjoy this book and I think everyone who is a fan of Hex Hall will like it. Sophie's story is wrapped up, and most loose ends are tied. I'm hoping, wishing, praying that if Hawkins ever revisits this world again, it's from Izzy's eyes. All of my disappointments come really from there, because a lot of that story isn't resolved. Plus, I want to hear the story with that mirror guy.<br /><br />Anyway, again, THANKS TO EVERYONE who liked or commented on my review. It makes me feel special and you all are awesome. Virtual chocolate chip cookies for everyone!!<br /><br />BTW, sorry for any spelling mistakes. <br /><br />Pre-Spell Bound<br /><br />A third Hex Hall. That means Demonglass will probably end with another cliffhanger. <br /><br />Oh, why can't Sophie and Archer be together!<br /><br />EDIT Mar 15: Yep. Another stinking cliffhanger. <br /><br />EDIT June 20: Oooo, it's called Spell Bound. Now if we can only up the release date... no? Fine, but I'm ready to see a cover people!<br /><br />EDIT August 9: Look at that sword! Sophie is going to kick some evil butt to get her Archer back! Yeah! (Though this cover is not nearly as epic as the Demonglass cover)<br /><br />EDIT March 13!!!:) I have it! Yay, yay, yay, yay! But darn it, I have all this college work that I should do before I read the book. So conflicted... </span>

<div id="review_1335538434" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1335538434" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer9460390805697948335"> <br/>I am <b> Spellbound. </b> Every time I read a book by a Rachel, it seems I am instantly captivated. Let me just recall some of these lovelies. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8440277.Rachel_E__Carter' title='Rachel E. Carter' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rachel E. Carter</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4728994.Rachel_Higginson' title='Rachel Higginson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rachel Higginson</a> and now <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2261547.Rachel_Hawkins' title='Rachel Hawkins' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rachel Hawkins</a>. Maybe it also has a lot to do with my awesome big sister being <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/37103769-rachel-maniacup' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rachel</a> too.<br/><br/>Now, now, let’s go to the review.<br/><br/>As much as I would like to say this is the best book in the series, I could not do that because honestly, compared to the first two, this is not as great but...there’s a <b>BIG BUT</b> (no pun intended. s</span>
  <span id="freeText9460390805697948335" style="display:none"> <br>I am <b> Spellbound. </b> Every time I read a book by a Rachel, it seems I am instantly captivated. Let me just recall some of these lovelies. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8440277.Rachel_E__Carter" title="Rachel E. Carter" rel="nofollow noopener">Rachel E. Carter</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4728994.Rachel_Higginson" title="Rachel Higginson" rel="nofollow noopener">Rachel Higginson</a> and now <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2261547.Rachel_Hawkins" title="Rachel Hawkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Rachel Hawkins</a>. Maybe it also has a lot to do with my awesome big sister being <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/37103769-rachel-maniacup" rel="nofollow noopener">Rachel</a> too.<br><br>Now, now, let’s go to the review.<br><br>As much as I would like to say this is the best book in the series, I could not do that because honestly, compared to the first two, this is not as great but...there’s a <b>BIG BUT</b> (no pun intended. seriously.), I am still very happy with how everything has been concluded in this finale.<br><br>What I love most in this series is how each character in the books has become really endearing. From the sassy heroine, Sophie, who never failed to crack me up, charming Archer, the quiet but heroic Cal, adorable Jenna and even the bitchy ghost, Elodie, the new characters (the Brannicks and even crazy Torin) and Sophie’s parents. All of them managed to make me laugh that they feel to me like really good friends and I just want to gather them all including Rachel Hawkins and myself in one big group hug. I’m so going to miss them. *sniffs*<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437034109ra/15529823.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>I am not overlooking the missing details in the plot such as the supposedly significant role of the Eye and the Brannicks in the story and how several events are quite downplayed a bit but the adventures the characters went through are still fascinating and engaging.<br><br>I wasn’t given an “epic finale” because that’s really highly unlikely and unrealistic because these books are more under the quirky, mushy, amusing type but I couldn’t think of better resolutions than those presented by the author. Even this character's death- I was like NOOOOOOO! at his death at first but eventually realized that it was acceptable and meaningful. <br><br>A happy ending is inevitable and I really liked it that everyone got some perks. Even the dead ones got theirs. Lol.<br><br>I could already imagine my friend, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/28640648-melissa-ever-so-mela" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa</a> saying "This, she prefers over <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15863832.Angelfall__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___1_" title="Angelfall (Penryn &amp; the End of Days, #1) by Susan Ee" rel="nofollow noopener">Angelfall</a>?" while rolling her eyes and smirking, definitely smirking and maybe even shaking her head. You influence me way too much, Melissa. Lol.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9460390805697948335" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katy" href="/user/show/4572741-katy">Katy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer295109409" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15889732667022976150">Was it just me or was anyone else truly and utterly disappointed with this book? I really, really, really liked the first two, but this one just didn't do it for me - not because Sophie didn't choose the guy I was rooting for but becasue the whole book itself was pretty blah.<br/><br/>First of all, I LOVED Sophie in the first two books. This one, not so much. She was just downright annoying. "Hellalicious? Duck, duck, demon? Brannicks, magic and hell, ohmy?" Really?!?! I know Hawkins was writing Sophie as</span>
  <span id="freeText15889732667022976150" style="display:none">Was it just me or was anyone else truly and utterly disappointed with this book? I really, really, really liked the first two, but this one just didn't do it for me - not because Sophie didn't choose the guy I was rooting for but becasue the whole book itself was pretty blah.<br /><br />First of all, I LOVED Sophie in the first two books. This one, not so much. She was just downright annoying. "Hellalicious? Duck, duck, demon? Brannicks, magic and hell, ohmy?" Really?!?! I know Hawkins was writing Sophie as a character that was trying to make light of the situation, but she was trying WAY to hard to be funny. And what's worse, it seems like Hawkins knew that and she would follow the cheesy comment ACTUALLY saying that Sophie was trying to make a joke of it or that Sophie grimmace at the sounds of that.<br /><br />The book itself was just okay. Don't get me wrong, there were a few good scenes in there, but most of it was blah. I was really bored definitely through the first part of the book until the guys showed back up (and no it wasn't because of the lack of romance) and pretty much up until halfway through the book. And the whole change from the Brannicks to Hex Hall and then to Ireland was just so choppy that it was disorienting, and splitting it up into Part 1, 2 and 3 didn't excuse it any less.<br /><br />As for the love triangle, don't even get me started. Do not click this until you've read the book because it does contain MAJOR spoilers.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[First of all, I've never been a big fan of Archer, even from book 1. He was arrognt, obnoxious and not very swoon worthy. And I didn't like that they called each other by their last names even after they became romantically involved. Believe me, I've had my fair share of favoring the bad boy or the jerk over the nice, sweet one. BUT I can't can't stand Archer. Sorry, no love lost there.<br /><br />I did like Cal, though I knew Hawkins would never write Sophie ending up with him. What I WAS disappointed in however, was the way Sophie treated him in this book. As if kissing him and then kissing Archer ten minutes after wasn't bad enough, Hawkins had to find SOME way to keep him romantically in the picture. So what better way to do it than use Eloise's possession to make it happen. Sure, just blame it on Eloise. Because Sophie didn't enjoy it. Because Sophie's not woman enough to go after the kiss herself. Because Hawkins can't have readers hating her. Absolutely CRUEL. So I was trying to figure out how Hawkins was going to write him out. Maybe give him to Finn? Maybe find him another love? Maube have him realize that she's not the right one for him. No, she had to off him. Too easy. Meanwhile Sophie continues her happily ever after with the asshat. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Sorry, maybe a little bitter about the whole thing.<br /><br />I can't say this was a bad book to read because it did have its moments. Unfortunately, it was NOWHERE NEAR as good or as intriguing as the first two. Truly sad to see a good series end like this.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer253668625" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5334162557377795795"><b><i>D'</i> Epic Battles</b><br/> <br/><i>Harry</i>'s version...<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380365983ra/718155.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><i>Aragorn</i>'s version...<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380365983ra/718156.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><i>Sophie</i>'s version...<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380365983ra/718157.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>There are lots of reasons why I gave it two stars or what we called <b>OK</b> stars rather than the <b>Liked</b> stars.<br/><br/>The Hex Hall has been highlighted or well known for its being fluffy, charming and funny. And that’s why I liked this series. This third book on the other hand is too darn dark to be neither these three. sigh!<br/><br/>Initially I had problems with the "<b>whole book</b>". I never felt fully immersed with it. I felt like a ping pong ba</span>
  <span id="freeText5334162557377795795" style="display:none"><b><i>D'</i> Epic Battles</b><br> <br><i>Harry</i>'s version...<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380365983ra/718155.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><i>Aragorn</i>'s version...<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380365983ra/718156.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><i>Sophie</i>'s version...<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380365983ra/718157.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There are lots of reasons why I gave it two stars or what we called <b>OK</b> stars rather than the <b>Liked</b> stars.<br><br>The Hex Hall has been highlighted or well known for its being fluffy, charming and funny. And that’s why I liked this series. This third book on the other hand is too darn dark to be neither these three. sigh!<br><br>Initially I had problems with the "<b>whole book</b>". I never felt fully immersed with it. I felt like a ping pong ball that constantly tossed from one side to another. There were twists and turns and lots of the snark that kind of didn’t flow well, mainly because there are so much going on and the storylines should have had more depth to them.<br><br>I really don’t want to spoil the story for you, but there’s a <s>slightly</s> darker feel towards the end of the book. I felt a bit cheated with Hawkins taken an easy way out to get to the ending that she came up with. And the big choices, highlighted moments and the final battle were a bit not so '<b>big</b>'. I’m all like '<i>Oh she easily repelled the power of the <b>mwahaha-evil</b>! Good for her.</i>' or more like '<i>that’s all will happen when you visited the underworld?</i>' Yeah in other word: <b>why the heck its way too easy with her?</b><br><br>As for the characters they are still likeable, especially Cal and Jenna. Both of them I think did grow from the first to this last book though I didn’t like what happened to one of them. For Archer, he’s still charming and all but he goes from <b>Mr. Hot</b> down to <b>Mr. Cute</b>. Maybe because he has smaller part in here and their (<i>Sophie-Archer</i>) love team didn’t give me sparks compare to <i>Sophie-Cal</i> love team. And now for Sophie<b>...</b> well, Sophie's character to my opinion is quiet overdone in this book. Don’t get me wrong, her humor has always been one of my favorite parts of the series, but it sometimes felt very out of place in the more tense situations here.<br><br>I think that, as a reader, I was just expecting so much more from this final book in the series since the middle book was just so good. Ah! Well Spell Bound was still a good book, it just wasn't a great book, at least it didn't <i>end</i> great.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2599653432955513069">I need this now!! "HOLY HELL WEASEL" ! Look at the purple on the cover! PRETTTTY. Want, want, want so much!<br/><br/>___<br/><br/><br/>"Holy hell weasel" perfection. Spell Bound is faultless and a brilliant ending to the series. I could not have asked for more.<br/><br/>Spell Bound picks up where we left off in Demon Glass... Well kind of. Sophie's powers have been sealed off and she now finds herself with the Brannicks. But they have a plan and Sophie is the key. Then, suddenly, Sophie finds herself back at Hex Hall and she'll n</span>
  <span id="freeText2599653432955513069" style="display:none">I need this now!! "HOLY HELL WEASEL" ! Look at the purple on the cover! PRETTTTY. Want, want, want so much!<br /><br />___<br /><br /><br />"Holy hell weasel" perfection. Spell Bound is faultless and a brilliant ending to the series. I could not have asked for more.<br /><br />Spell Bound picks up where we left off in Demon Glass... Well kind of. Sophie's powers have been sealed off and she now finds herself with the Brannicks. But they have a plan and Sophie is the key. Then, suddenly, Sophie finds herself back at Hex Hall and she'll need the help of Jenna, Cal, and Archer to defeat the evil demon raising Casnoffs.<br /><br />I fell in love with all of these characters in Hex Hall and throughout Demon Glass and to Spell Bound my love for them all just continued to grow. I adore Jenna and think she's a fabulous best friend. I adore Cal and totally want him for myself. I adore Sophie's family. I adore the villains and friends. I'm in love with Archer Cross and his arrogance and sexiness. And mostly, Sophie Mercer. Who is a protagonist full of wittiness, who's heart is always in the right place, who is powerful and overall brilliant.<br /><br />It's an ending not without sacrifice, but where I still sighed with complete happiness when I was done. I couldn't have asked for a more enjoyable and witty series. I loved every part of the Hex Hall series and I cannot praise Rachel Hawkins enough for it.<br /></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=read-only-when-running-out-of-book">read-only-when-running-out-of-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=young-adult-books">young-adult-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=i-hate-love-triangle">i-hate-love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=nothing-special">nothing-special</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer535735596" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9509681366127818764"><i>Pre-review:<br/><br/>Am I the only one who have grown to dislike Sophie and think she's becoming increasingly annoying during the first two books?<br/><br/>Am I the only one to think Ms. Hawkins' supposed 'humor' and witty remarks are getting old? <br/><br/>Am I the only one who thinks witty remarks are nice, but if they were spoon-fed to us in almost every single page of a novel, then I will have to say 'enough is enough'?<br/><br/>In another words, I don't have much high hope for that third book of the series.</i><br/><br/>Short Review:<br/><br/>1.5 star.<br/><br/>I</span>
  <span id="freeText9509681366127818764" style="display:none"><i>Pre-review:<br><br>Am I the only one who have grown to dislike Sophie and think she's becoming increasingly annoying during the first two books?<br><br>Am I the only one to think Ms. Hawkins' supposed 'humor' and witty remarks are getting old? <br><br>Am I the only one who thinks witty remarks are nice, but if they were spoon-fed to us in almost every single page of a novel, then I will have to say 'enough is enough'?<br><br>In another words, I don't have much high hope for that third book of the series.</i><br><br>Short Review:<br><br>1.5 star.<br><br>I have a feeling that Ms. Hawkins was either not being serious, or she simply had stopped caring about her own story and characters when she wrote Spell Bound. I can't even feel she had been making any effort to make her book decent, and I hate it when authors get lazy. What a disappointment!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380409571i/802002._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(Link to original photo: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://vampirekiki.deviantart.com/art/listen-to-Ruki-266124378">http://vampirekiki.deviantart.com/art...</a>)<br><br>Authors, write your books with care, don't be lazy! I dislike lazy authors as much as the bad ones!<br><br>Sophie continues to be annoyingly and unnecessarily witty and filled with smartass remarks in this book, <b>whilst the evil witches had already launched their attack, people are dying and her daddy, best friend and love interests are missing in a burning building.</b> Still need me to say more about her? It may be okay for a character to make light of the serious situation once in a while, but for an entire book? Are you kidding!?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380409571i/802003.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The structure of the book is also problematic, we shifted from one scene to another so rapidly that I feel like the entire novel is being shabbily chopped up and then thrown messily back together; or it's like Ms. Hawkins had too many ideas but she was in too much a hurry and she only had the space of one book instead of two to tell her tale.<br><br>Plus there're a lot of things just conveniently happen in Spell Bound. For example, Elodie's ghost conveniently shows up now and then to use magic when Sophie's own magic is sealed off. The evil villains talk freely about how they plan to control Sophie and use her as a weapon <b>right in front of Sophie herself</b>. Can you see what it is? Lazy writing. <br><br>Talking about Elodie, I'm super disappointed by how she was handled by Ms. Hawkins from book 1 to book 3. I mean, in Book 1 Hex Hall, Elodie and her fellow witches killed a classmate and framed another, and throughout an entire book none of those witches showed the tiniest hint of guilt for what they had done. No one snapped or broke down because they were feeling sorry or scared. There're only two possibilities for their behaviors: (1) Elodie and her friends are extremely cold blooded and irredeemable, or (2) Hex Hall isn't as well written as everyone had made it sound.<br><br>And then in book 3, Elodie becomes oh-so helpful, what's her motives? Why are she helping Sophie now? Wasn't she supposed to hate normal humans enough to try calling up a demon before? So why is she now okay with Sophie's attempt to stop the evil witches from hurting humans? Zero explanation. Hawkins didn't bother to even bring these up.<br><br>Just as lazy and ridiculous is Sophie's trip to <i>Hell</i>. That part of the story reads like Hawkins wrote this book for 5 years old kids, not young adults who know better.<br><br>As to the ending, I simply don't give a damn, but the death of a certain character still angers me...<br><br>As a whole, it looks like Ms. Hawkins didn't care about her book anymore when she penned Spell Bound. Maybe she thought: <i>"Since the first two books are selling so well, my readers will surely be buying the last book of the series regardless of the quality!"</i> So here we are, with a badly written final book being shoved to us. <br><br>I think if the Hex Hall series is about a girl discovering that she's a witch and tries to deal with being a witch instead of a girl finding out not only she's a witch BUT ALSO A SUPER-SPECIAL WITCH, THE ONLY ONE OF HER KIND WHO'S GOING TO FIGHT THE EVIL WITCHES AND SAVE THE WORLD. I would have been a lot happier with this series.<br><br>The one good thing about Spell Bound is that it's a quick read, it wouldn't charge you much. If you need a book to kill time, you may also try.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9509681366127818764" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1535241360983621280">I'm not sure how long has it been since I've read Demonglass, but while reading this one, it felt like it has been too long.<br/>It's like my brain lost it's ability to remember details from previous books and at some times, I was lost.<br/>I forgot names, relationships and some pretty big events that happened before this book.<br/>However, page by page, I remebered most of it.<br/><br/>This was an okay last book in the series.   <span id="freeText1535241360983621280" style="display:none">I'm not sure how long has it been since I've read Demonglass, but while reading this one, it felt like it has been too long.<br />It's like my brain lost it's ability to remember details from previous books and at some times, I was lost.<br />I forgot names, relationships and some pretty big events that happened before this book.<br />However, page by page, I remebered most of it.<br /><br />This was an okay last book in the series. It was not an epic finale and I can't even call it a conclusion since it left open door for a spin-off that, as far as I know, will not be happening any time soon (if ever!).<br /><br />The writing style is really good. I had fun reading Sophie's sarcastic comments. She has the best humor style you could ask from a book character.<br /><b>This series is the funniest paranormal book series I have read so far.</b><br />I enjoyed reading it and now I'm looking forward to start Hawkin's other series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8475505.Rebel_Belle__Rebel_Belle___1_" title="Rebel Belle (Rebel Belle, #1) by Rachel Hawkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Rebel Belle</a>.</span>

<div id="review_315834814" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/315834814" />
    <a title="Jonababez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6105268-jonababez"><img alt="Jonababez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554850504p2/6105268.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/315834814?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jonababez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jonababez" href="/user/show/6105268-jonababez">Jonababez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6105268-jonababez?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer315834814" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2095207818057386952">I finished reading this book last night, and I needed to calm down before I write a review. (This contains few spoilers, so watch out!) I'm too depressed, too sad, and too frustrated. I know I should have not taken this book so personally, but I've grown to really like Cal, and it has hurt me damn much on what has happened to him. He didn't deserve it. It was too much. I hate Hawkins for doing it to him, she didn't even give him a chance to be happy. And I also hate myself because I'm so affecte</span>
  <span id="freeText2095207818057386952" style="display:none">I finished reading this book last night, and I needed to calm down before I write a review. (This contains few spoilers, so watch out!) I'm too depressed, too sad, and too frustrated. I know I should have not taken this book so personally, but I've grown to really like Cal, and it has hurt me damn much on what has happened to him. He didn't deserve it. It was too much. I hate Hawkins for doing it to him, she didn't even give him a chance to be happy. And I also hate myself because I'm so affected. I know, this is not about Sophie and Archer since he's out of the picture already, but hey, why did he has to die? I don't really get the point there. Anyway, I was also hoping that Hawkins will write a little love story between Cal and Elodie, but no! It didn't happen! Just a slight comment from Elodie about making Cal change his mind about her.<br /><br />Yeah, this whole review is all about Cal, and not about the book, but I hope you'll understand my sentiments and I'm seriously grieving right now. It'll take me a whole bunch of happy books to cheer up. Maybe if I'm not this sad anymore, I can give a proper review. LOL!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2095207818057386952" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katherine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katherine" href="/user/show/4356179-katherine">Katherine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4356179-katherine?shelf=magic-powers">magic-powers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4356179-katherine?shelf=werewolves-wolfes-shifters">werewolves-wolfes-shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4356179-katherine?shelf=dissapointed">dissapointed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4356179-katherine?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4356179-katherine?shelf=faery-fairy-fey">faery-fairy-fey</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4356179-katherine?shelf=witches-warlocks">witches-warlocks</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer262729397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13943922937278965924"><u>RATING: 2 Out Of 5</u><br/><br/><b>Major. Let. Down.</b><br/><br/>How un-surprising that the last novel in the Hex Hall series would be a major let down and be utterly disappointing. Eghh its infuriating some of the events that transpired in the novel and readers you’ll know exactly what I’m talking about when you read it. <br/><br/>The novel is un-funny – though it does try very hard to be so, but I’m afraid it falls short in the funny department. Looks like Hawkins used up all her cans of funny in the previous two books, and these bo</span>
  <span id="freeText13943922937278965924" style="display:none"><u>RATING: 2 Out Of 5</u><br /><br /><b>Major. Let. Down.</b><br /><br />How un-surprising that the last novel in the Hex Hall series would be a major let down and be utterly disappointing. Eghh its infuriating some of the events that transpired in the novel and readers you’ll know exactly what I’m talking about when you read it. <br /><br />The novel is un-funny – though it does try very hard to be so, but I’m afraid it falls short in the funny department. Looks like Hawkins used up all her cans of funny in the previous two books, and these books cannot survive without the funny. The funniness is what makes these books. This is the first major down fall.<br /><br />The second is the story line, it’s just kind of jumbled and rushed and doesn’t feel right. It feels like Hawkins has just made up stuff and chucked it in there just to chuck it in there, not caring if it actually fits right into the story. Also Sophie I loved in the previous two novels, in this book however I did not, she did so many things I don’t agree with and made her very unlikeable. I’m just amazed how a book series that started off amazing ended up so crappy and silly? Perfect example of this though is the Strange Angels series, same problem.<br /><br />The other major let down is the big impending battle in the end. Yer it’s not a big battle at all. It goes for 14 pages!!!! That’s it; the big battle that was built up in every novel goes for 14 pages!! Was the most stupidest boringest battle ever, they don’t even defeat the big evil themselves, they have <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ her sister to thank for that, imagine if you guys actually had to fight someone yourselves, you guys would have your arses handed to you on a plate <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Oh and yer they go to the underworld and oh that’s excited and is explored... yer no – under 10pages. So many times Hawkins could have explored and delved into deeper many of the things she introduced in the novel but she doesn’t, instead she filled the book with boring and not needed/unnecessary scenes. <br /><br />I think Cal is the most unlucky character in the world, he is constantly getting f***ed over in every book and this book is no different, with this one being the worst of the them all with...<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Cal getting to finally make out with Sophie, or so he thinks, it’s actually Elodie possessing her body. So Cal is f***ed over by that. Secondly, Hawkins kills him off!!! He already had a shit existence throughout the novels; with him seeing his fiancée go off with someone else, and instead of giving him a nice happy ending – because he deserves it – YOU KILL HIM OFF!!! Not fair. Poor Cal. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And there you have it. The last novel, is the let down of the series and such a dissapointment. Oh well, it only took me a day to read, so not that much is lost.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13943922937278965924" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1340909144" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5265420690078424517">Wow! This series really is enchanting!No wonder,I was also bewitched in Rachel Hawkins' School Spirits which is clearly btw not a sequel to Hex Hall,nor Hex Hall is a sequel to School Spirits.But both have a different kind of entertaining stories where in the other series,you'll find the story of Izzy(Isolde) while the other is about Sophie.<br/><br/>I can't believe that the newly introduced characters here were actually the characters I was missing in School Spirits,(though they were already mentioned in</span>
  <span id="freeText5265420690078424517" style="display:none">Wow! This series really is enchanting!No wonder,I was also bewitched in Rachel Hawkins' School Spirits which is clearly btw not a sequel to Hex Hall,nor Hex Hall is a sequel to School Spirits.But both have a different kind of entertaining stories where in the other series,you'll find the story of Izzy(Isolde) while the other is about Sophie.<br /><br />I can't believe that the newly introduced characters here were actually the characters I was missing in School Spirits,(though they were already mentioned in Hex Hall) but I never thought they'll play an important role in this final book!How amazing,right?<br /><br />So when I've found out that these new characters have a major connection with Sophie, I got even more excited and couldn't help admiring how brilliant RACHEL HAWKINS is for creating this very unique,enthralling story.<br /><br />In this final sequel,Sophie and her allies have come to work and plan together on how would they get Sophie's power back,and end the evilness of their enemies.<br /><br />There were also shed-tears moments in the story,especially on the death of one charater here and it did devastate me.But then,it was an honorable death that would make you respect and love this particular character even more.<br /><br />The ending I must say though is a bit abrupt, but I did enjoy reading it 'cause "Sophie Awesome Sparkle-Princess" is so hilarious! Just to prove that,let me share you some of her dialouges that totally cracked me up:<br /><br />**- "Why would there be soup in-oh,"supes"?Like for supernaturals?"<br /><br />**- "Jackass,jackass on the wall,where's the info on Hex Hall?"<br /><br />**- "We could go to Lough Bealach",Aislinn said and Sophie asked,"Is that a place or are you choking?"<br /><br />Until now,those lines make me laugh everytime I read them so yes, the ending is still fantastic! I just felt a little sad when I'm done reading it because I know,I will deeply miss the characters including Elodie,who I adored here in this final sequel,Izzy,Finley,Aislinn and Torin again(glad to see them here).<br /><br />I never reread the books that I've already read,but this series had totally got me and I'm sure,I'm going to reopen this one day. And so yes, now I absolutely agree with my little sister Aj that "RACHEL" indeed is a lovely and a fantastic name!lol^^<br /><br />So my fellow readers,don't ever miss this series!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6688000362964616300"><br/>I have to say and with no little surprise on my part but this was actually fun!<br/><br/>I really enjoyed the writing. Not a lot of points for the story cause let's face it, nothing actually ever wraps up with such a neat and pretty bow. It was very sunshine and rainbows and HEAs which is cool, sometimes you need uncomplicated and simple to ease your mind.<br/><br/>And that's what this book did. Finishing it, I felt all light and happy. I loved Soph's parents, like a lot. Not big on her boyfriend and best friend bu</span>
  <span id="freeText6688000362964616300" style="display:none"><br />I have to say and with no little surprise on my part but this was actually fun!<br /><br />I really enjoyed the writing. Not a lot of points for the story cause let's face it, nothing actually ever wraps up with such a neat and pretty bow. It was very sunshine and rainbows and HEAs which is cool, sometimes you need uncomplicated and simple to ease your mind.<br /><br />And that's what this book did. Finishing it, I felt all light and happy. I loved Soph's parents, like a lot. Not big on her boyfriend and best friend but her parents totally made it worth it. :p<br /><br />Also, I get she saved the world and all that but who in their right mind makes a seventeen year old the leader to their race?! Granted I have a very low opinion about the younger generation but no. This was probably the only thing that bugged me, silly I know. xD<br /><br />And this is what happens when I lose the internet for a day. I finish three books and start and finish another a couple hours later. Lol.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer578516158" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer7413489514377517721">First thing first. I love the ending. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Though, happy endings are too mainstream, it seems to me that the ending of the third installment of this book, this whole trilogy was heart-warming and pure happiness. I can picture Sophie smiling, holding the hands of Jenna and Archer, also smiling too. <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><br/>The story has started when Sophie enter the Itineris and came up in the Brannicks homestead and in just that particular beginning, a revelation has shocked Sophie. Me too. I re</span>
  <span id="freeText7413489514377517721" style="display:none">First thing first. I love the ending. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Though, happy endings are too mainstream, it seems to me that the ending of the third installment of this book, this whole trilogy was heart-warming and pure happiness. I can picture Sophie smiling, holding the hands of Jenna and Archer, also smiling too. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The story has started when Sophie enter the Itineris and came up in the Brannicks homestead and in just that particular beginning, a revelation has shocked Sophie. Me too. I really have no idea that was possible, but after reading it, okay, I accept it. More revelations had come to my way, about the Brannicks, Sophie herself, and others that really froze my mouth gaping.<br /><br />In this final installment of Hex Hall, I am really relieved and happy that it didn't en route to a wrong turn. It is now clear to me who are in the bad side and who are in the good side. Our characters were still awesome and the new characters were also likable, especially Izzy and Torin. Sophie, I still really loved Sophie. She grew stronger and wiser. Her sarcasm was given, no doubt on that. She never failed to amuse me with her snarky dialogues and wittiness. Elodie's character was also very important in the book. One just can't underestimate her.<br /><br />My issues about the book are: <br />1. The blurb says there is an epic war but I guess there is none. The war was plain simple, I'm afraid. I don't want to elaborate but I didn't read an epic war, just fighting.<br /><br />2. The information about The Eye and the Brannicks are lacking. I want to know more.<br /><br />3. The adventure to the Underworld is quite fast. I am hoping that they will encounter something demonic but no. (Though what they experienced is quite demonic too)<br /><br />4. Some characters were not explained who really they are.<br /><br />Indeed, this is still a very good book that will bring you an abundance of laughter and a bunchful of tears. Though my issues with the book, other events are still breath-taking, heart-pounding, riveting and will cause you to stab the antagonists to death.<br /><br /></span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer206519540" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16393445565101982076">Popcorn! If I had to pick a mood-food to go with these books it would have to be a big buttery bowl of popcorn. <br/>It just goes so nicely with the theme of entertaining and fun as hell!<br/><br/>I'm gonna keep this brief since really all I have to say is that I freaken love this series!!<br/>It's fun and funny, it's exciting and completely consuming. It doesn't have one dry moment. I love the writing and the zingy dialog. The characters are incredibly easy to love, the romance is giggly swoon-worthy and the story</span>
  <span id="freeText16393445565101982076" style="display:none">Popcorn! If I had to pick a mood-food to go with these books it would have to be a big buttery bowl of popcorn. <br />It just goes so nicely with the theme of entertaining and fun as hell!<br /><br />I'm gonna keep this brief since really all I have to say is that I freaken love this series!!<br />It's fun and funny, it's exciting and completely consuming. It doesn't have one dry moment. I love the writing and the zingy dialog. The characters are incredibly easy to love, the romance is giggly swoon-worthy and the story-line is one big heart-pound. <br /><br />There was only one moment I could have lived without, and anyone who has read this already knows what that one moment was, so I wont bother spoiling it. If it wasn't for a certain scene at the very end of the book, I probably would have given this a 4/4.5 star but I thought that was sincerely a nice touch and it made my heart happy even though it was still something that I wish could have been avoided instead. <br /><br />Yeah, so other then that, I absolutely loved this! I'm sad to see one of my most beloved series go, but I look forward to seeing what Hawkins has in store for us next!</span>

        <a title="ℓуηη, ℓσкιѕℓутнєя¢ℓαω" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ℓуηη, ℓσкιѕℓутнєя¢ℓαω" href="/user/show/9804517">ℓуηη, ℓσкιѕℓутнєя¢ℓαω</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781423153634" href="/book/show/13258839-spell-bound">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9804517?shelf=fantasy-ya">fantasy-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9804517?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9804517?shelf=need-to-own-asap">need-to-own-asap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9804517?shelf=trilogies">trilogies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9804517?shelf=love-triangles">love-triangles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9804517?shelf=seriously-underrated">seriously-underrated</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2600076558" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2045189760115871829">I'm rather sorry that this is the last book. This has been an extremely entertaining & hilarious series! Definitely putting itself up there with my favs. I'm still mad at myself for letting it sit on my tbr like for SIX while years, which is as long as I've been on Goodreads. That's really sad lol<br/><br/>Anyway, this installment gets a <b>4.75 stars</b><br/><br/>As always, you can totally depend on Sophie to bring all the epic snark and sass, and witty lines when she's nervous. That's one of the things I love most about</span>
  <span id="freeText2045189760115871829" style="display:none">I'm rather sorry that this is the last book. This has been an extremely entertaining &amp; hilarious series! Definitely putting itself up there with my favs. I'm still mad at myself for letting it sit on my tbr like for SIX while years, which is as long as I've been on Goodreads. That's really sad lol<br /><br />Anyway, this installment gets a <b>4.75 stars</b><br /><br />As always, you can totally depend on Sophie to bring all the epic snark and sass, and witty lines when she's nervous. That's one of the things I love most about this series is it's hilarity at all times. It's such a light-hearted &amp; fun read to brighten the dreary winter weather. <br /><br />Another thing I love about this book (and series) is that there's never a dull moment. There's no plot holes, plot sags &amp; useless fluff shoved in for filler. It just erupts with endless action, jokes, suspense, etc. Everything there is there for a reason! Those are the best kind a of books 📚<br /><br />Other things I loved:<br /><br />Elodie, has become a surprising favorite for me. In book one I <b>never</b> would have believed it possible, but omg I adore this girl!! She's all spice and fire and fun. With book two I grew to like her. But this book is where I loved her. That is an amazing bit of writing on the author's part to make us hate a character and then turn around and <i>love</i> her. *Fist bump Miss Hawkins* 👊<br /><br />I absolutely loved the relationship growth between Sophie &amp; Elodie. They go from pitted enemies in book one and then by the end of the series develop an unexpected friendship. It was just beautiful growth throughout the books. <br /><br />I also loved how, despite their differences, beliefs, and feelings, that Archer, Cal, Jenna, Sophie, and Elodie worked together to take down the evil bitches of the story. They looked out for each other and pushed each other to succeed.<br /><br />There were quite a few unexpected twists that happened on the way through this book. Not all of them I loved, but I did love the fact that I was surprised. Another sign of great writing. <br /><br />Here are some of the shockers:<br /> 1) Cal <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ dies saving Sophie. I'm SOOO not okay with this. Cal was my favorite guy of the love triangle, and I totally didn't foresee the author resolving the drama of said triangle by killing one of the trio off. Just wow. I was thinking this whole time that Cal was just too good and sweet for this world. Apparently the author foretold my thoughts.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> 😱😭💔<br /> 2) The Brannicks <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ helping Sophie and her crew of Prodigium misfits, or taking in her demagicked dad. I did guess her mom was a Brannick, but I think that was obvious with how book two ended <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /> 3) Mrs. Casnoff <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ would help Sophie end the horrors on Graymalkin Island by bringing her sister to get &amp; knocking herself &amp; Lara into the evil pit <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /> 4) Nick <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ turns out to be Archer's cousin, and it was HIS parents who killed Archer's. And it was Lara who turned Nick's parents cause they were close friends  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> 👿<br /> 5) Elodie's <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ reluctance for Sophie to untether their bond. I totally didn't expect Elodie to admit they were friends. That was so sweet!!! Like omg all sugary and warm!! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> 💚😊<br /><br />Something I did really like, that was a result of earlier spoilers, but this one I seriously hoped for and kinda exoected, and thankfully Miss Hawkins delivered <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Cal comes back as a ghost. And he seems to retain some of his white witch power cause he's slowly healing Graymalkin Island of all the gray and decay the Casnoffs caused. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It's so bittersweet, but I <i>needed</i> this for proper closure on this series after that climax of drama. 😥💜😭<br /><br />And as always with this series, there were essences of Harry Potter here and there, sprinkled throughout. And it was done tastefully &amp; not in a total copy-cat unoriginal way like some authors have the tendency to do.<br /><br />One of two things I didn't like were <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ how easily Sophie broke free of Lara's mind control. I mean I know Sophie is super strong, buuuuut it just seemed to easy, especially after all the hype that was placed on it. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And then of course I still wasn't satisfied with how the love triangle turned out. I mean both guys are great in their own ways, but I was definitely rooting for one over the other. So that's why I docked a fraction of a star 🌟<br /><br />I <b>
  <i>highly recommend</i>
</b> this series to everyone!! It's so much fun to read! And it's hard to put down at times. Well, most of the time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2045189760115871829" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_201526401" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/201526401" />
    <a title="Mimi Valentine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6110599-mimi-valentine"><img alt="Mimi Valentine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314137947p2/6110599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/201526401?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mimi Valentine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mimi Valentine" href="/user/show/6110599-mimi-valentine">Mimi Valentine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=best-of-2012">best-of-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=boys-i-wish-were-real">boys-i-wish-were-real</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=pure-awesomeness">pure-awesomeness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=finished-copy-for-review">finished-copy-for-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer201526401" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17782384578118517322"><b>Rating:</b> 4.5 out of 5 stars!<br/><br/>I don't want to write this review. Instead, I want to hide in the corner with a blanket and some tissues so I can read this book all over again because: It. Was. AMAZING! <br/><br/>Taking place right where <b>Demonglass</b> left off, <b>Spell Bound</b> starts off running and doesn't slow down at all. Every time you think that something is going right and the cast will finally get a break, something else goes wrong that leaves you flipping pages faster than before. Hawkins knows how to write a</span>
  <span id="freeText17782384578118517322" style="display:none"><b>Rating:</b> 4.5 out of 5 stars!<br /><br />I don't want to write this review. Instead, I want to hide in the corner with a blanket and some tissues so I can read this book all over again because: It. Was. AMAZING! <br /><br />Taking place right where <b>Demonglass</b> left off, <b>Spell Bound</b> starts off running and doesn't slow down at all. Every time you think that something is going right and the cast will finally get a break, something else goes wrong that leaves you flipping pages faster than before. Hawkins knows how to write a one-sit read, and she proves it a million times over with this book! <br /><br />Sophie has to be one of my favourite heroines of all time! She's the Queen of Snark, the demon you want as your best friend, the kind of girl you can count on... but most of all, she's <b>real</b>. So much happens during the span of this book — and this entire <i>series</i> — that causes her to continue to grow yet still remain the same fantastic girl we know and love. <br /><br />This review wouldn't be complete without mentioning the boys. ♥ I love Archer because his snark matches Sophie's in a way that makes him perfect for her, and he has that sort of bad-boyish feel to him that all girls love. But Cal — who pulls off the strong, silent, yet really sweet healer like no one else — will do some things that will completely win over your heart. <br /><br />My only complaint is that there's one HUGE plot twist near the end that I felt wasn't touched on enough! I wanted closure; I wanted recognition; I wanted time to <i>cry</i>, damn it, because it blew me off my feet even though the rest of the end felt perfect in its own way. <br /><br />Finales are always hard to swallow because sometimes you're too emotional over the end to feel anything else, but Rachel Hawkins managed to craft a brilliant end to a brilliant series! <b>Spell Bound</b> is as fast-paced, fun, and awesome as I thought it would be, yet it was also intense, gripping, and heartbreaking too. My recommendation for this series is sky high! <br /><br /><b>BUY or BORROW?:</b> If you don't have this series on your shelf yet, I have nothing to say to you except to buy it! These books are perfect if you want to read something fast or fun or just plain awesome. I LOVE having them all on my shelf! :)<br /><br />(Original review at <a href="http://diminutivemimi.blogspot.ca/2012/03/review-spell-bound.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Mimi Valentine's YA Review Blog</a>)</span>
  <a data-text-id="17782384578118517322" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_187043517" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/187043517" />
    <a title="Sarah Mac" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4490376-sarah-mac"><img alt="Sarah Mac" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499925811p2/4490376.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/187043517?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Mac" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Mac" href="/user/show/4490376-sarah-mac">Sarah Mac</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=zzz-2012">zzz-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=uber-disappointing">uber-disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=read-regifted">read-regifted</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=zzz-departed-ya">zzz-departed-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer187043517&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer187043517" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11571558686320038974">It wasn't terrible beyond belief, but I didn't connect with it. I enjoyed the interaction between Sophie & Elodie, & Torrin was a decent side character. I didn't even mind Cal's resolution, per se.<br/><br/>But guys, the forced humor. The inappropriately timed snark. The constant barrage of lame-ass jokes. ENOUGH. STFU. Sophie barely opens her mouth unless it's to say something humorous (or the author's version thereof). True, Sophie has always been a smartass, but in the past she knew when to shut up & b</span>
  <span id="freeText11571558686320038974" style="display:none">It wasn't terrible beyond belief, but I didn't connect with it. I enjoyed the interaction between Sophie &amp; Elodie, &amp; Torrin was a decent side character. I didn't even mind Cal's resolution, per se.<br /><br />But guys, the forced humor. The inappropriately timed snark. The constant barrage of lame-ass jokes. ENOUGH. STFU. Sophie barely opens her mouth unless it's to say something humorous (or the author's version thereof). True, Sophie has always been a smartass, but in the past she knew when to shut up &amp; be serious. I didn't see that here -- which is odd, given the serious undercurrent of the plot. Likewise, it doesn't seem like her relationship with Archer has matured since the other books, &amp; I agree with another reviewer who asked why the council would give her such a position of power when she's barely 17. And speaking of power...what's with that battle for control of her demon-self? All that yammering build-up for TWO F'ING PAGES? C'mon. Talk about brushing a significant moment under the rug.<br /><br />Overall, it felt as if the author dumped all her leftover plot-bunnies into a Vitamix &amp; blended into 300-page gravy. For all that goes on in <i>Spellbound</i>, it should have been twice as long as the others. The first section rushes through revelations about Sophie's mom (yawn) &amp; crams in a useless cameo from Sophie's dad (that's it? really?), before shoveling everyone back to school...only to have them escape yet again &amp; make an utterly WTF journey to the Underworld -- the possibility of which has never been mentioned until <i>halfway through</i> this particular book. (Deus-ex-machina? Your knickers are showing.) Follow that with a spottily-described epic battle &amp; some help from the all-knowing Tome O' Magical Awesomeness (aka more deus-ex-machina)...yeah, not feeling it.<br /><br />My conclusion: the author bit off more than she could chew with three fast-reading novels that were geared toward a younger YA audience. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11571558686320038974" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ABlfBFgvYmVREwKY8Si43NvVyaropesaVv127+fZRYQvJHG82dF3rZuvMvLJPr+WirDPR96rBRlKaGQxgBeCJQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('B5FeLJRsXWPD066uxdZAVjfZUhOKRIT0rQNc0Ahk0A0orHCUFZJIqwlvnsT9wEccZrxU/rxKavexlk4Ob6oXrA==')})
  }
//]]>
